***** Data Set meanings
    | set   | meaning                                                 |
    |-------+---------------------------------------------------------|
    | t0    | n11 + new delay_sum timing info write                   |
    | e0    | t0 + energy ratios wM=0.5, wE=0.4, wD=0.1               |
    | mp    | t0 + Xavi's MFCC's copied to PLP stream                 |
    | m0p   | t0 + Xavi's MFCC's copied to PLP stream, mfcc_weight==0 |
    | e0w   | e0 + [[/homes/scotto/meetings/xclust/exp/run/run.00016/mergedRunInfo.dump][combinatorial]] wM, wE, wD weight runs               |
    | e0wOv | e0w+overlaps                                            |
    | t0wOv | t0+overlaps                                             |
    | e1nr  | t0 + eratios, combinatorial weights w/o ovdet           |

    | delxs0        | weight combinations of Xavi's xc w/ NR & mine w/o NR                    |
    | de120         | new xcpair.cpp format, stores 20 peak loc/vals                          |
    | de120xs       | del20 with Xavis' viterbi smooth                                        |
    | de14xs        | 4 delay peaks stored, with Xavis' viterbi smooth, no wiener             |
    | erNr          | noise reduced eratios                                                   |
    | erNrC         | mix of eratios on PLP channel and eratios concat on MFCC's              |
    | erNrCp        | mix of eratios on PLP channel and eratios concat on MFCC's, some PCA'ed |
    | xcNr          | del4xs + wiener noise reduction                                         |
    | xcNoVit       | del4xs, no Xavi viterbi filtering                                       |
    | erCxcC        | new confidences (xcpair.cpp version 1.28, eratio.cpp 1.12)              |
    | erCxcC.5      | erCxcC but 0.5s instead of 1s xc winlen                                 |
    | NRall.xc5     | noise reduction on both ER and XC, 0.5s XC,ER windows                   |
    | xc5           | no noise reduction on either ER or XC, 0.5s XC,ER windows               |
    | NRall.xc1.0   | noise reduction on both ER and XC, 1.0s XC window, 0.5s ER              |
    | erNRxcN0.x5   | NR on ER, no NR on XC, 0.5s wins on both                                |
    | erNOxcN0.x5   | no NR on ER, no NR on XC, 0.5s wins on both                             |
    | erNRxcN0.x1e1 | NR on ER, no NR on XC, 1s wins on both                                  |
    | erNRxcN0.x1e5 | NR on ER, no NR on XC, 1s win ER, 0.5s XC                               |

************* DONE [[file:~/meetings/contrib/icsi/BeamformIt/functions.cpp::Global_delays_decoding%20config][Global_delays_decoding()]]
              Finds two least cost paths through the top two peaks of all
              correlation pairs.  Number of combinations is 2^npairs (huge for
              lots of channels) so limits search to block_size groups of
              pairs.  Note that the last block can be up to size
              2*block_size-1, not block_size (this means 9 pairs ==> 2&9
              combos ==> 512 combos

* [[ASRU]] Paper (due 7/16/07) cvstag=asru07_submit :cvstag:
*** final submitted paper cvs version: 1.4 :cvs:
*** Overlap oracle experimentss					    :conclusion:

    Exclude overlaps from scoring, and then exclude them (or not) from
    clustering; if overlap detection improves diarization, you could hope
    that the scores would be higher when they have been excluded from
    clustering. This test wouldn't catch the possibility that results would
    be better during overlap.  This /would/ show up in the [[model import oracle]]

    - 4073 vs. 4077: assign1 almost as good as perfect

      before clusering
    - 4101 vs. 4102, mfcc's: assign1 is 1% worse than perfect
    - 4104 vs. 4112, mfcc's: 1.4% improvement if remove before ==>
      /xcpairs improves robustness to overlaps/ ! 
 
*****  _nearest-2 overlap fillin does well_	:conclusion:
*****  _100% accurate overlap detect doesn't help_single speech much_ :conclusion:
*****  _XC's may help single-speech model building overlap robustness_ :conclusion:

***** Mari's overlap assignment question answers
      ([[file:~/meetings/xclust/seldom_used/ovAssignSurvey.m]])
      (ran over run.4116 output)

 | ovNbdAssign | medianDur |  pctDur |  num |   pctNum |
 |-------------+-----------+---------+------+----------|
 | all         |      0.32 |     100 | 4840 |      100 |
 | lr          |     0.115 | 12.2146 |  808 |  16.6942 |
 | sameNotLR   |    0.3465 | 87.6059 | 4028 |  83.2231 |
 | otherNotLR  |     0.949 | 0.17952 |    4 | 0.082645 |

ovNbdAssign:

    all:  all overlaps
    lr: the assigned overlaps are the speakers to the left and right of the overlap
    sameNotLR: nearest-2 did not assign the left right speakers because they were the same speaker
    otherNotLR: nearest-2 did not assign the left right speakers for some other reason (edge cases)

medianDur: median overlap time for this case (s)
pctDur: percentage of overlap time consumed by this case
num: number of times this case occurred
pctNum: percentage of overlap occurances for this case.
***** Code for experiments
      
      _Clusterer Input_:

      If option _noOvClustIn_ is set, overlaps are removed from VAD rttm and
      reference rttm's [[file:~/meetings/xclust/xclust.pl::refRttmFNm%20ref_rttm_file%20opt%20mtngNm%20rttm][here]], which is accomplished with a call to
      [[file:~/meetings/xclust/remOvSegs.pl::if%20clustOutOvAct%20eq%20assign1][remOvSegs.pl]], with no special flags.

      _Scoring_:

      If option _diarClustOutOvAct_ is set, overlaps are removed from scoring
      [[file:~/meetings/xclust/xclust.pl::remOvSegsDir%20refDirTmp%20tmpdir%20clustOut][here]], with a call to [[file:~/meetings/lib/MtngLib.pm::sub%20remOvSegsDir][MtngLib::remOvSegsDir()]].  The nearest-2
      replacement is done by modifying RTTM's with a call to [[file:~/meetings/xclust/remOvSegs.pl::if%20clustOutOvAct%20eq%20assign1][remOvSegs.pl]],
      with the flag '--clustOutOvAct assign1'

******* need this maybe for PPCA overlap det too
******* not necessary for XC's if do PPCA beamformer
******* Xavi says it's needed
******* One of the [[conferences]] I added after ASRU had PCA/ICA as a topic
******* See[[ PCA/CCA/KPLS dimension choice]]
***** [[MDS coherence]] mic distance est.
******* a possible input to:
********* confidence (far means low conf)
********* overlap detector (a confidence in having detected an overlap)
********* delay est (modern TODOA, channel selection)
*********** shrink eigen or corr window by using dist as delay offset
*********** remove very distant pairs
********* energy ratio (remove too-close pairs)
******* steps
********* use references to select non-speech 
*********** middle intensities? remove speech, keep noise SNR high
*********** only use long nonspeech segments
*********** remove collar around edges to avoid missed VAD
********* calc pair coherence (averaged)
*********** how average?, compute it over an X sec window so can view stability)
*********** [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::mccowan06arrayShapeMDSnoise][McCowan et al. 2006: Microphone Array Shape]]: 
************* nfft=2048, 50% overlap and alpha = 0.65, fs=16KHz
************* 100 noise frames before stable dist est.
************* ~13s noise only frames
************* they just picked the lowest energy frames
*********** frequency range: just go from DC to Nyquist (maybe notch 60, 50Hz?)
************* too high: electronic noise dominates, but it never does, probably

                [[http://www.massa.com/fundamentals.htm][freq dep atten up 50KHz]]:
                  a(f) = 0.01f
                  a: max atten (vs. humidity) in dB/ft
                  f: KHz
                  am(f) = 0.01 * 0.3 * f = 3e-3 * f

                So, atten @ 3m and 8KHz = 72dB

                [[http://www.larsondavis.com/PreamplifierDataSheets/PRM903-1203_D0501_0022_RevB.pdf][Microphone electronic noise]] (outdoor mic, maybe a crappy
                one):  

                 noise=3.7uV, peak voltage is 14v

                 ==> best case SNR = 14/3.7e-6 = 131dB


                 Worst case would knock off @ most 40dB (factor of 100
                 gain)

************* not sure how low is too low, but want to avoid 60Hz hum?
************* chohereDist_test.m rev 1.2 shows substantial gain in accuracy if include f<60Hz
*************  *go from DC to Nyquist, just like McCowan*
*********** complex coherence from FFT's won't be real
************* phase rotates around, is random, imag will be comparable to real
************* could take magnitude
************* could just take a bunch of samples like McCowan and pick the best fit
************* From [[http://citeseer.ist.psu.edu/361561.html][here]] (ref'd by McCowan), looks like take Re(complex_coherence)
********* [[1http://www2.imm.dtu.dk/hbn/immoptibox/][Levenberg-Marquadt]] for fitting coherence to distance
*********** Note: I just coarsely sampled distances
********* MDS
*********** Matlab [[http://www.mathworks.com/products/statistics/demos.html%3Ffile%3D/products/demos/shipping/stats/cmdscaledemo.html][Classical MDS]] (cmdscale())
************* convert genetic distances into 2D coordinates

              Interesting way of entering upper triangular adjacency data:

              D = [4.69 6.79 3.50 3.11 4.46 5.57 3.00 ...
                        2.10 2.27 2.65 2.36 1.99 1.74 ...
                             3.78 4.53 2.83 2.44 3.79 ...
                                  1.98 4.35 2.07 0.53 ...
                                       3.80 3.31 1.47 ...
                                            4.35 3.82 ...
                                                 2.57];  

              Makes a 1x28 vector (main diagonal is zero so not entered,
              this is the form output by the Matlab pdist command)
              
              use squareform(D) to create a square, 8x8 matrix

************* use procrustes command to align w/ known geographic coords 
              (compute rotation/scale/offset to best match in LMS sense)
************* cmdscale (matlab MDS) on Euclidean distances is identical to PCA, up to a sign change

*** self-confidence learning
    1. cluster
    2. new per-frame "truth" by  using cluster GMM's
       - no time constraints, allows bad individual frames
       - nonspeech in frames is exposed
       - overlaps are exposed
    3. train pairwise GMM's
       - GMM inputs contain confidence features for all pairs, not just
         this one
    5. ID error's against new per-frame truth
    6. get confidence by training a pairwise error predictor
    7. cluster with confidences

*********** Pre-image reconstruction (problems and improvements)

            _Summary_ Reconstructing from feature space started out hard,
            very slow, and not necessarily unique.  Original techniques
            above solve a complex iterative optimization problem based on
            min reconstruction error.  I'm looking for a unique, closed
            form technique.  Shape algorithms are good if they save
            rotation, etc..  Eiegen voice papers are good if they have
            simple reconstruction, and are also interesting if they compute
            posteriors in feature space.  Wiener filter is there because it
            suggests a way to do use TDOA

            _Read these first_

************* Polynomial Kernel is invertible sometimes ([[http://www.wisdom.weizmann.ac.il/~vision/courses/2003_2/KernelBasedMethods.ppt][Kernel Based Methods]])
              
              Polynomial kernel
                
                k(xi,x,) = (xi . xj + c)^d;   (

              is invertible when c>=0 && d is odd (formula on slide 64).
              But is entropic more important? ([[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Williams02kpcaAndMMDS][Williams 2002: Connection between Kernel]])

************* Overview: [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::scholkopf99InVsFeatKern][Scholkopf et al. 1999: Input space versus]]
              - input/feature space review
              - some explanation of KPCA
              - analytical expression for preimage calc that I can't
                figure out how to use
              - polynomial, signmoid and RBF kernels are invertible
              - a recursive pre-image algorithm for Gaussian kernels
************* TODO Need to compare the three algorithms below
************* TODO (maybe do this) [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Bakir04LearnPreImage][Bakir et al. 2004: Learning to Find Pre Images]]
              - highly [[http://scholar.google.com/scholar?q=Learning+to+Find+Pre-Images&ie=utf-8&oe=utf-8&rls=org.mozilla:en-US:official&client=firefox-a&um=1&sa=N&tab=ws][cited]]
              - supposedly easy to implement
              - calculates transform once, rather than once for each space
              - s/b easy to sample lag manifold this way
              - seems simple enought to do (ridge regression)    
              - but PICKS THE WRONG DIGIT!?
              - might want to replace ridge regression w/ something better:
                - [[http://theoval.sys.uea.ac.uk/matlab/default.html][heteroscedastic ridge regression]]
                  - link includes matlab ([[http://theoval.sys.uea.ac.uk/matlab/hkrr_demo/hkrr_demo.m][hkrr_demo.m]]) and [[http://theoval.cmp.uea.ac.uk/~gcc/publications/pdf/neurocomp2004a.pdf][paper]]
                  - demo has leave-one-out crossvalidation param tuning
                  - this gives you error bars ==> _confidences_?
                - support vector regression
                  - [[file:~/lib/matlab/svm/svr.m][svr.m]] and [[svroutput.m]] (example of use in [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ccaDimPickTrain.m::yout%20svroutput%20thisB%20B%20leaveOutI%20ker%20beta%20bias][ccaDimPickTrain.m]]
                  - evaluates fewer support vectors.  s/b much faster than KRR
************* TODO (maybe) [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Rathi06statShapeKPCA][Rathi et al. 2006: Statistical shape analysis]]
              - Closed form approx to inverse, unique and no iteration
              - only self-cites
              - esp. useful b/c only uses feature space (so I can twizzle
                and scan lags for SRP-PHAT)
              - not sure this will work b/c I want to go down to 1-D and
                this alg. assumes that the PCA approx was a good match in
                feature space.  This might not be true.
              - Seems simple enough to try
************* TODO (maybe) [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Kwok04kernPreImage][Kwok & Tsang 2004: pre image problem]]]]
              - closed form, linear algebra
              - works on feature space distance (what I really want, I think)
              - some stuff here explained better in  [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Williams02kpcaAndMMDS][Williams 2002: Connection between Kernel]]
              - seems simple enough to try, but MDS step might be
                unnecesary (see the other options above)
              - I don't like the nearest neighbors picking stuff.  For
                lags, might have enough samples with bad lag pairs that the
                badness will be accurately reproduced, even for low PCA
                dims?
************* [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Rathi06statShapeKPCA][Rathi et al. 2006: Statistical shape analysis compare]]
              - closed form pre-image
              - some nice pictures of bones, seems worth reading

************* [[http://citeseer.ist.psu.edu/zhang04probabilistic.html][Probabilistic Kernel Principal Component Analysis]]
************* [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/xpls/abs_all.jsp?arnumber=1495480][Kernel Eigenvoice Speaker Adaptation]]
              - interesting b/c calc's probs in feature space
************* [[http://www.cs.ust.hk/~mak/PG-Thesis/thesis-roger.pdf][Kernel Eigenspace-based MLLR Adaptation]]
              - explains which kernels are invertible (to pre-image)
              - calc's posterior w/o needing to do inverse problem (like PPCA)
              - [[http://citeseer.ist.psu.edu/mak04improving.html][improved]] since
              - extended to multiple regression classes eg. [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/xpls/abs_all.jsp?arnumber=1415281][here]]
************* [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/search/srchabstract.jsp?arnumber=1628697&isnumber=34164&punumber=10843&k2dockey=1628697@ieeecnfs&query=%28%28kernel+wiener+filter+using+canonical+correlation+analysis%0D%0Aframework%29%3Cin%3Emetadata%29&pos=0][Kernel Wiener Filter Using Canonical Correlation Analysis Framework]]
              - iterative reconstruction algorithm
              - CCA TDOA? half CCA mimimized MSE between CCA X and Y channels
************* [[http://www-rocq.inria.fr/who/Hichem.Sahbi/Web/Papers/cbmi05.pdf][Affine Invariant Shape Description Using The Triangular Kernel And Its Application To Leaf Recognition]]

              - bad: recognizes "shape": invariant to translation, rotation, not scale
              - uses a triangular window

*************** John says this is *slow*

********* [[www.ee.technion.ac.il/~rmeir/Publications/KrlsReport.pdf][Kernel Recursive Least Squares]]
*********** method for linear prediction eg. applied to equalization
*********** is on-line (kernel matrix is sparsified so OK for large data sets) 
*********** selects a new dict, vect. when pt. not well-projected onto current set
*********** closely related to kpca
************* large corr matrix, C, eig vecs are almost entirely projected onto dict. 
************* but kpca projects onto 1st M ortho eigen vecs
************* KRLS doesn't diagonalize C so doesn't get exactly orthog comps.
************* is way cheaper than kpca
************* relation to [[greedy kpca]]?
*********** MATLAB [[http://www.eecs.umich.edu/~wingated/resources.html][here]] 
********* [[http://www.techfak.uni-bielefeld.de/~sklanke/][Unsupervised Kernel Regression]]
*********** a method for learning principal manifolds
*********** has matlab and C

***** Delay and Filter beamformer
******* Advantage of using delay and filter (max or min eigenvectors)
********* Filters allow lower sample rate
*********** If I'm bandpassing, to 3KHz, it's dumb to have Fs=16Khz (could be 6-8KHz)
*********** but this would coarsen the delay
*********** BUT, filters allow fractional delay, probably can get the resolution when you're averaging many samples
*********** NOTE: lower sample rate also reduced the # of taps needed for Eigencomp or the # of FFT bins if do freq domain eigen stuff
********* Filters handle reverb and mixing, of course
******* Freq domain eigenvectors/filter (helps w/ long eigen filters??)
********* [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Warsitz05filtSumBFpca][Warsitz & Haeb-Umbach 2005: Acoustic filter and]]
*********** eigen problem in each DFT bin
********* [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::WarsitzPartFiltAdaptBF][Warsitz: Adaptive Beamforming Combined]]
*********** uses above, plus particle filter speaker dynamics
*********** NOTE: BF filt is 40X longer than max delay diff (close mics)
*********** For me, I have _giant_ lags ==> _giant_ filter, maybe why it won't work for me?
*********** But, since the eigen dimensions are small (Nchans choose 2), maybe this is more doable than eigenvecs in time
*********** This would allow me to have a long filter via a long FFT w/o increasing eigenvalue problem at all!
******* Eigenstuff can go into PPCA ==> a prob model ==> no peak picking!

*** Why bad ER w/ eval07 configs? (/answer: do_feat_weights==1/)      :conclusion:
    (as I reported in WASPAA07/ICASSP08 papers)
***** Chuck's eval07 options table (from: 070504_status.lyx)

      | config option   | Chuck eval07 | Xavi eval06 | Meaning                                         |
      |-----------------+--------------+-------------+-------------------------------------------------|
      | do_feat_weights |            1 |           0 | do BIC stream weights in merge decision         |
      | do_frame_purify |            0 |           1 | try to de-weight non-speech in clusters         |
      | do_fren_init    |            0 |           1 | do BIC clust init (alternative is linear)       |
      | do_num_clusters |            0 |           1 | automatically select initial number of clusters |
      | min_duration    |          250 |         300 | min speaker segment size                        |
      | weight_del      |         0.35 |        0.10 | HMM stream weight delays                        |
      | weight_mfcc     |         0.65 |        0.90 | HMM stream weight for MFCC's                    |


      - Agglomerative clustering merge decision is made using a normalized
        BIC metric, with fixed stream weights calculated over each
        segment to be considered for a merge. Previously the merging was done
        using data likelihoods weighted by fixed stream
        weights. Re-segmentation is still being done with fixed stream
        weights.

      - During merging, an attempt is no longer made to detect and remove
        non-speech. This gives me another chance to improve results using
        feature confidences.

      - Reduce the minimum speaker segment size from 3s to 2.5s, better
        matching real utterance minimum durations.

      - Select a fixed number of initial clusters by linear segmentation
        (instead of employing a BIC-based algorithm, with the number of
        initial clusters depending upon the size of the training data).

      - Greatly increased the influence of location features.

***** go back to original good ER results for mixed ER/XC features: [[file:~/meetings/doc/reports/status/061025_status.pdf][061025_status]] 
      (some went into Interspeech07 paper)

        _Conclusions_  

        1.) I'm still not getting my fabulous 10.8% result on rt05se w/
            eval06 configs. I'm getting 14.13, which still beats the baseline
            substantially.  *Why?*
        2.) Yes, the new config breaks ER+xdel
        4.) rt07 config w/o do_feat_weights, rt07 config hurts both plain ER
            and ER+xdel (both)
        5.) inconsistency!  run 4500 s/b same as 4538: I changed the config
            file loading code to make sure stuff is overwritten: assuming no
            bugs, is something that wasn't overwritten before now being
            overwritten?
        6.) rt07 - weights seems like the best ER perf (4494 vs. 4536, or
            4528 vs. 4529)
        7.) *do_feat_weights==1 breaks ER's*  _So turn it off_

        _Conclusions_

        1. /do_feat_weights==1 hurts perf (3 streams, or ER doesn't meet XC assumptions)/
        2. PCA'ed XC and ER in separate streams doesn't seem to be a good
           strategy 
        3. adding XC stream helps ER performance over ER-alone
        4. best ER dim:     ER.mP2
        5. best weights: 0.8/0.1/0.1
        6. best ER nmix: 5
        7. tiny changes in dev perf can imply big changes in test perf
           eg. the two do_feat_weihts==0 dev runs above

*** CCA (2 loc stream: locfeats in 2 HMM streams, both CCA'ed, do_feat_weights==1) :conclusion:

    _Conclusion_: 
    Using both MFCC and ER smoothing of XC's yields a small
    perf gain over the best single loc stream CCA approach (compare with
    runs [[05046]]/[[05065]]).  Also, do_feat_weights==1 may be OK for a 3 stream
    HMM; the problem may be that it effectively assumes a single Gaussian
    (see [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Anguera07tdoaAcoustWeights][Anguera et al. 2007: Automatic Weighting for]]).  Finally, it's
    intersting that the optimal weights put more emphasis on MFCC
    smoothing, agreeing w/  [[05046]]/[[05065]] showing that MFCC smoothing was the
    most reliable.

********* mutual information of pairs w/ class labels clust outs almost same as refs :conclusion:
          See [[file:~/meetings/xclust/pairMutInf.m::clear%20all][pairMutInf.m]]
*** feature picking (see also [[Mutual information with cluster ID]])   :conclusion:
***** maximum relevance min redundancy (mRMR)			    :conclusion:
      ([[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::peng05featSelMutInfo][Peng et al. 2005: Feature selection based]], [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::ding03featSelMinRedund][Ding & Peng 2003: Minimum redundancy feature]])
******* NumChans-1 features, like Xavi                              :conclusion:
********* same weights as Xavi raw feats			    :conclusion:

        _conclusions_: Peng's redundancy diff works the best (but I haven't
        test the quotient), and uniform priors is an improvement upon
        Peng's non-weighting (in every case).  Mutual information alone works the
        worse, so removing redundancy is important.  Finally, it's possible
        that GCCPHAT is better. To test, I'd need to run w/ gccphat and my
        pairs instead of Xavi's.

***** max(min(channel SNR) pairs                                    :conclusion:
      
      _Conclusion_: SNR not a good way to pick channels (but see [[zero SNR
      channels]]).  It's not so terrible on the test set for XC's, but is
      awful on the dev set and for ER's

******* how to run
        generate channel sel filed: [[file:~/meetings/xclust/calcSNRall.pl::Generates%20files%20needed%20to%20select%20channels%20based%20on%20max%20min%20channel%20SNR][calcSNRall.pl]]

        produced, and w/ opt [[file:~/meetings/xclust/xclust.pl::stepM%20setOpt%20qw%20pickFeatSNRvers%20pickFeatNmeth][pickFeatNmeth]] set to [[file:~/meetings/lib/MtngLib.pm::if%20pickFeatNmeth%20eq%20nChM1][nChM1]]
******* zero SNR channels
        The SNR program had several meetings with zero SNR, which is bogus,
        but I think I remember the author saying that this meant that the
        channel was bad.  In any case, I sorted pairs with zero SNR
        separately, by sum(SNR), so that if there was one strong channel in
        the pair, it would get ranked higher in the selectio

* Overlap Detect
*** Detection
***** Features
      - time to next unique speaker (either direction)
      - width of current segment?
      - entropy in sliding winT
      - relative fit of top two models
      - relative fit of ID'ed model and nearest-2 model
***** Assumptions
******* Speech is always detected, even if it's overlapped
******* Overlap is always the two nearest speakers
***** Properties of overlap
******* Poor model fit 
********* model entropy, MFCC's, ER's, XC's
********* likelihood is lower than usual for a given speaker model
******* Should be a good match to both of nearest-2 speakers?
******* Focusing on two speakers should improve MFCC fit (also shading?)
***** Implementation
******* *typFitLik*: don't match as well as the ID'd single speaker GMM typically does in rest of the meeting

        foreach feat
          foreach win
            likDiff(win) = GMM(feat,spkrID(win)) -
                           mean(GMM(feat,spkrID(allwins))) / std(GMMliks(spkr))
          end
        end

******* *typFitEnt*: generally weak model fit (GMM entropy for each feature)
******* *near2FitLik*: should have good match to both nearest-2 GMM's (nonfocused)

        take advantage of the fact that one or the other speaker dominates
        (W-disjoint orthogonaility).  This might work better for loc feats,
        esp. XC than for MFCC's

        foreach feat
          foreach win
            % assign frame to max lik nearest 2 speaker
            foreach frame(win)
              frameID(frame)=maxlik(GMM(feat,nearest2(spkr)))
            end

            ovfeat(win) = difference between liklihoods of sorted frames
                          and the likelihoods typical for nearest 2
          end
        end
                      
******* *near2LocCompFit* some loc feat pairs (GMM dims) may match one of the 2-nearest speakers
        (do this for both er's and XC's)

        foreach speaker
          foreach mic pair
            GMM(spkr) <-- pair lags for that speaker

        foreach sliding window, win
          foreach mic pair
            likID = lik(GMM(spkrID'd),win,pair,)
            foreach nearest-2 neighbor
              likID -= lik(GMM(neighbor),win,pair)
            end

            likDiff(pair) = likID/std(lik(GMM(spkr),allsegs))
          end

          feature(win) = sum(likDiff);
        end

******* *near2FocusFitLik*: MFCC's should match better than when focused on nearest 2 spkrs

        Be sure to use Xavi's correlation weighting idea!

        foreach spkr
          likGmmBase(spkr,allwins) = likGMM(GMM(spkr),baselineMFCCs,allwins)
          foreach comp (GMM(spkr))
            MFCC = calcMFCC(focus(comp))
            likComp(spkr,comp,allwins) = lik(GMM(MFCC,spkr,comp),allwins)
          end
        end

        foreach win
          % should match better than at least one nearest 2, probably both
          featPlain(win) = figurethisout(GMM(spkrIDed(win)),GMM(nearest2))

          foreach comp (GMM(spkrIDed(win)))
            lik1(nearestSpkr,comp)=likComp(nearestSpkr,comp,win)
          end

          for nearestI=1:2
            nearestSpkr=nearest2(spkrIDed(win),nearestI);
            foreach comp (GMM(nearestSpkr))
              lik2(nearestSpkr,comp)=likComp(nearestSpkr,comp,win)
            end
          end

          feat(win)=figurethisout(lik1,lik2)
        end

******* _Functions_

        findNearest2()
        calcLiks() (share w/ dim reduce picking)
        typicalFitCompare()
        modelEntropy()
        nearest2GMMfit()
        nearest2locFeatCompFit()
        focusMFCCfit()
        
******* Scripts to run:
********* [[file:~/meetings/clustloc/associateFiles::usr%20nikola%20bin%20perl%20w][associateFiles]]
          makes filenames, loads them into the filename database
********* [[file:~/meetings/xclust/mkOvVadRefs.pl::usr%20nikola%20bin%20perl][mkOvVadRefs.pl]]
          converts RTTM's to vad ref information, also extracs delay
          triplet info and maybe some other stuff
          
********* [[file:~/meetings/xclust/vadModels.pl::Trains%20an%20overlap%20detector][vadModels.pl]]

          generates a sil/spch1/ov GMM set for use in removing nonspeech
          frames from data considered to be speech by the diarization
          clusterer

          _outputs_: 

          [[file:~/meetings/xclust/vadModels.pl::liks%20ovGMMpost%20out%20mtng%20vadOvGMMlik][<ovVadMfccGMMpost out $$mtng{vadOvGMMlik}>]]

          MFCC vad output (sil/spch1/ov)

********* [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovdetFeats.pl::usr%20nikola%20bin%20perl][ovdetFeats.pl]]
          Makes Hough features, delay triplets, model fit entropies

          _inputs_: 
          ovGMMpost: from vadModels.pl (used to remove nonspeech)

********* [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovdetTrnTst.pl::usr%20nikola%20bin%20perl][ovdetTrnTst.pl]]

          ]]trains overlap detector GMM's and MLP

          _outputs_:

          [[file:~/meetings/xclust/vadModels.pl::][<ovGMMpost out $$mtng{vadOvGMMlik}>]]
          (overlap detector posterior)

***** Overlap feature vector definition (overlap model fits only)

      determined in two places: 

      1.[[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::outNms%201%20silSpchVadLikRat][ovModFitFeat.m]], as called by [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovdetFeats.pl::step%20cmd%20ovModFitProg%20outFNm%20ovModFit%20out%20mtng%20feat%20ovdetModFitFeatFNm][ovdetFeats.pl]]

        - [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovdetFeats.pl::feat4FNm%20datVerFeat4%20in%20mtng%20feat%20streamIn_feat4FNm][streams]] are feat4 (delays) and mfcc's
        - [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::featFNm%20feat4%20opt%20feat4FNm][model input feature order]] is mfcc:feat4
        - [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovdetFeats.pl::ovEnt%201%20if%201%20include%20model%20entropy%20in%20ovModFitFeats][entropy]] is included
        - vector per feature is:

          [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::out%20maxLikSpch%20vprobs%201%20clue%20to%20classifier%20about%20whether%20is%20speech][silSpchVadLikRat]]: clue to classifier about whether is speech
          [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::out%20out%20mrgThisNNmax%20mrgThisNN][mrgThisNNmax]] 
          [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::out%20maxLikSpch%20vprobs%201%20clue%20to%20classifier%20about%20whether%20is%20speech][mrgThisNN
          ]][[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::out%20out%20ent][ent]]
          
        - at the end of the feature is: [[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovModFitFeat.m::out%20out%20mrgThisNNmfcc%20mrgThisNN][mrgThisNNmfcc+mrgThisNN]]

        - so the total ovModFitFeat feature vector is:

          silSpchVadLikRat
          mrgThisNNmax.mfcc
          mrgThisNN.mfcc
          ent.mfcc
          mrgThisNNmax.feat4
          mrgThisNN.feat4
          ent.feat4
          mrgThisNNmfcc+mrgThisNN

      2.[[file:~/meetings/xclust/ovdetTrnTst.pl::fNmFile%20fNmFile%20tmp][ovdetTrnTst.pl]], where mfcc, feat3/4 and triplets are merged 

      ovModFit features are plotted in [[file:~/meetings/xclust/test/ovDetError_plot.m::featNms%20arrayfun%20x%20sprintf%20feat%20d%20x%201%20size%20feats%202%20UniformOutput%20false][ovDetError_plot.m]] (no MFCC's or triplets)

      run [[8250]] is an ovModFit+mfcc run

      ovModRemIdx=[2,3,4,7,8] means locfeats-based ovModFit features only;
      otherwise it's mfcc modFitFeats only

      _conclusion_: locfeats do not seem to help

***** Oracles

      ref rttm's -->|ovsegs (rttm?) (call $MtngLib::segs2vad)
                    | nearest-2 speaker indices (true ones) |
                                               
      clust rttm -->|nearest-2 speaker indices (what you'd get in real life)

      ref rttm's -->|speaker |
      features   -->|GMM liks|--> likframes (htk, per model)

      likframes  -->|calc |
      nearest2   -->|feats|--> entropy,likdiffTypical,likdiffN2 (per model)

      ovsegs     -->|

***** Speaker model entropy
***** confidence features ([[file:~/meetings/clustloc/xcpair.cpp::outFrms%20startFrm%200%20maxPkNormR12][xcpair.cpp]])

    outFrms[startFrm+0] = maxPkNormR12;      // maxXCpeak / sqrt(pairower)
    outFrms[startFrm+1] = maxPkNextRatioR12; // maxXCpeak / next highest XC pk
    outFrms[startFrm+2] = pkEntR12;          // BROKEN: s/b normalized by log(nPks)
    outFrms[startFrm+3] = pitchPkRatio;  // strong peak in pitch region 
                                         // (spatial alias, not sure if useful)
    outFrms[startFrm+4] = pitchPeriod;   // maybe helps MLP figure stuff out?

***** HTK training
******* HTK review
********* files
*********** .phn: each row: startT endT label  (ex: [[file:/g/ssli/data/timit/dist/test/dr1/faks0/sa1.phn::0%209640%20h][sa1.phn]])
*********** .scp: each row is a .phn filename (ex: [[file:~/oldresearch/timit/labs/origlabs_test.scp::g%20ssli%20data%20timit%20dist%20test%20dr1%20faks0%20sa1%20phn][origlabs_test.scp]])
*********** .scp: column 0 == source column 1 is dest (ex. [[file:~/oldresearch/timit/flists/raw2mfcc.scp::g%20ssli%20data%20timit%20dist%20train%20dr1%20fcjf0%20sa1%20wav%20n%20nest%20b0%20scotto%20timit%20features%20train%20dr1_fcjf0_sa1%20mfcc][raw2mfcc.scp]])
*********** .mlf: of .phn files w/ filename tails (ex. [[file:~/oldresearch/timit/labs/phlabs_train.mlf::MLF][phlabs_train.mlf]])
*********** .dic: list of phones (2 cols so can remap?) [[file:~/oldresearch/timit/labs/timitphones.dic::sil%20sil][(ex. timitphones.dic]])
*********** .hled: describes the phone mappings (ex. [[file:~/oldresearch/timit/phmap.hled::Map%2061%20Phone%20Timit%20Set%2048%20Phones%20HTKBook%20p%2092%2093][phmap.hled]])

***** Overlap speaker model fits
******* comparing GMM probs / entropies
        
        Take likelihood ratio and average over window vs averaging over
        window and then finding the top two ratios?  Also, individual mixtures?

        _Conclusions:_
        1. when calculating whole GMM, averaging 1st and then taking the
           ratio is best
        2. when looking at individual mixtures, it's better to take the
           ratio 1st
        3. mfcc's work the best (but not well)
        4. Surprisingly mfcc's work for mixtures
        5. removing nonspeech from ratio window helps 
           1. GMM's in A. vs. B. below
           2. However, scoring changed: scored only spch frms in ref
              RTTM.AND detected by clusterer.  B/F was just all ref...
        6. Nearest neighbor helps for MFCC's, doesn't hurt for locfeats (C.)
        7. ent is crappy again (C.)
        8. crossEnt is crappier (D.)
        9. merged model vs. max single model works better than 2 single
           model comparisons (E); NN best for loc, mrgTop2 slightly best
           for mfcc 10.GMM vad prefilter helps a little bit (F. vs. E.)
        10. 2 sec max window expand is about right (G,H, runs of system F
           w/ 1s and 4s were a little worse)
        11. crossent w/ feat4 works better than w/ feat3 (H. makes sense b/c
            feat3 is already CCA'ed w/ MFCC's, will have less unique information)
        12. mrgThisNN product is worse than (H, mfcc * feat4)
        13. 
           
        14. mrgThisNN product s/b sum of log ratios, not prod (K, and is better
            than either by themselves).  Note that prefilter VAD was
            retrained in K, so the numbers are slightly different than previously.
        15. Ov classifier needs GMM level speech/nonspeech detector input:
            Ov ratios eg. mrgThisNN tend to be high during sil. that is (L)
            included in clusterVAD

* Dimension Reduction
*** What dimension?
***** See [[Number of PCA (or CCA) components]]
***** varies w/ clustering stage?
******* for ER/XC, should be fewer dims as clustering segregates speakers
        ==> redo dim reduction before making merging decision?
*** [[Feature Confidence]] and dimension reduction
***** problem w/ confidences processed by dim reduction ordinary is that per-band confidences go away
***** [[Feature Confidence]] in transformed subspace
***** scalar for each transformed dimension, want:
******* big if important pairs for this dimension had large confidences
******* "important": large magnitude element in transforming eigenvalue
******* transformed confidences ~ [0,1]  ie. probability-like
******* don't have to sum to one for each feature vector (may have all
        bad elements)

        ==> linear feature transform should have all positive
        coefficients 

        ==> can just normalize the selected subspace
        transforming coeffs to sum to one (but not really necessary)
***** [[http://glossary.computing.society.informs.org/second.php?page=A.html][affine transform]]:  coeffs sum to one??
******* affine transform [[http://mathworld.wolfram.com/AffineTransformation.html][definition]]:
        An affine transformation is any transformation that preserves
        collinearity (i.e., all points lying on a line initially still
        lie on a line after transformation) and ratios of distances
        (e.g., the midpoint of a line segment remains the midpoint
        after transformation). In this sense, affine indicates a
        special class of projective transformations that do not move
        any objects from the affine space R^3 to the plane at infinity
        or conversely. An affine transformation is also called an
        affinity.

        Geometric contraction, expansion, dilation, reflection,
        rotation, shear, similarity transformations, spiral
        similarities, and translation are all affine transformations,
        as are their combinations. In general, an affine transformation
        is a composition of rotations, translations, dilations, and
        shears.

        While an affine transformation preserves proportions on lines,
        it does not necessarily preserve angles or lengths.
******* [[http://www.imt.liu.se/~magnus/cca/tutorial/][Canonical Correlation Tutorial]] ([[http:www.imt.liu.se/~magnus/cca/tutorial/tutorial.pdf%20][pdf]]) says it's a translation of the origin followed by a
        linear transformation.
        - has matlab [[http://www.imt.liu.se/~magnus/cca/][here]]
******* note: [[file:~/prosbreak/doc/TODO_prosbreak.org::*use%20CCA%20for%20syntactic%20acoustic%20feature%20dimension%20reduction][use CCA for syntactic/acoustic feature dimension reduction]]?
***** [[Non-Negative CCA]]
***** Confidence weighted PCA
******* Good way #1: [[NPPCA]] accommodates measurement variance
********* see NPPCA section to see [[better error targets]] for conf trn idea
******* Good way #2: insert confidence into the PPCA EM gaussians, like I did w/ autoseg2.5
******* *Simple hack:* PCA is weighted sum: weight data one more time w/ confidences
******* weighted PCA (search this file for more weighted PCA stuff)
********* [[http://takane.brinkster.net/Yoshio/p057.pdf][weighted PCA]]
********* weighted PCA also done in robust PCA/SVD work [[http://www.salle.url.edu/~ftorre/papers/rpca2.html][here]] other robust stuff too
********* See [[PCA combined with feature selection (weighted PCA)]]
******* [[http://www.merl.com/papers/docs/TR2002-24.pdf%20][Mitsubishi incremental SVD w/ missing values]]?
********* binary missing/not missing: would have to threshold confidences
********* would possibly make the transformation better
******* alternative hack would be to just exclude vectors w/ low total
        confidence from PCA/LDA calc?
********* but this might bias the transform to easy cases...
********* maybe just want to let conf in GMM handle it?
******* [[http://www.google.com/codesearch?q=+weighted+principle%5C+component%5C+analysis+show:DzrKZ8Q9ijI:Xj_xNVTmcoM:ngVgHD_mr9A&sa=N&cd=3&ct=rc&cs_p=http://www.ph.tn.tudelft.nl/~csp/da/prtools315.zip&cs_f=prtools3.1.5/klm.m#a0][KL transform]] (uses posterior class probs somehow)?
********* /actually/ KLT is just PCA.  See the [[www.imt.liu.se/~magnus/cca/tutorial/tutorial.pdf%20][CCA Tutorial]]
********* a way to take confidences into account before doing the transform
********* pfile_klt does this

***** PCA reconstruction error as confidence (overlaps won't fit but is PPCA model fit better?)
***** DONE do meeting-wide PCA on /speech only/ to avoid noise
******* probably doesn't help: see [[VAD in PCA or not]]
***** DONE # pca dims vs. variance for whole meeting and per speaker
******* hints at whether should insert PCA in merging step

***** PCA
******* PCA/SVD Review
********* [[http://public.lanl.gov/mewall/kluwer2002.html][SVD and PCA Tutorial]] (from genetics, also has [[http://arxiv.org/ftp/physics/papers/0208/0208101.pdf][pdf]]):
*********** SVD
************* X=USV'
              X: mxn, the data
              U: mxn, is orthonormal basis for Xcols; Ucols are 
                 "left singular vectors"
              S: nxn, only nonzero along diag, diag has "singular values"
              V: nxn, is orthonormal basis for Xrows, rows are 
                 "right singular vectors"
************* square X: SVD is same as diagonalization ie. solving eigenval prob
************* Xapprox = sum(ucol(k)*s(k)*vrow(k)'), where k=1:nSingVals
*********** PCA (partly from [[http://www.dgp.toronto.edu/~aranjan/tuts/pca.pdf][another tutorial]] that includes SVD)
************* PXc=Y
              Xc: mxn, the data after the mean has been removed (column-wise?)
              Y:  mxn, the transformed data
              P:  mxm, the transforming matrix, Prows (princ comps) are
                  basis of Xcols
************* P is selected to point to orthogonal directions w/ max variance
************* is calculated from the eigenvecs of the Xc covar matrix: Xc*Xc'
************* for correlation-PCA, divide by each dim's variance b/f eig calc
*********** SVD vs. PCA
************* V'=eignenvecs(XX') if X==Xc ie. V' are the princ comps
************* U'=eigenvecs(XX') if X==centeredByRow(X)
************* (Also see "Relation to Principle Components Analysis," [[http://public.lanl.gov/mewall/kluwer2002.html][here]])
*********** SVD dim reduction
************* eigengenes: rows of V
************* i_th row of U contains the gene coordinates when mapped to eigengene space
************* throw away eigenengenens (reduce k) and you have dimension reduction
************* [[http://www.answers.com/topic/singular-value-decomposition][Reduced SVDs]]: 
*************** Three kinds
***************** Thin SVD
******************* /do QR decomp first/ if n<<m (nFrms<<nDim)
***************** Compact SVD
******************* calc vecs for 1st r eigs, more economical than thin if
                    r<<n (matrix is of rank r)
***************** Truncated SVD
******************* only vecs for larges r eigh vals: _what I want to do_
*************** With LAPACK or GSL:
***************** [[Computation%20of%20the%20SVD][Computation of the SVD]]

                  The LAPACK subroutine DGESVD represents a typical approach
                  to the computation of the singular value decomposition. If
                  the matrix has more rows than columns a QR decomposition is
                  first performed. The factor R is then reduced to a
                  bidiagonal matrix. The desired singular values and vectors
                  are then found by performing a bidiagonal QR iteration,
                  using the LAPACK routine DBDSQR (See Demmel and Kahan for
                  details).

                  The GNU Scientific Library offers three alternative ways to
                  compute the SVD: via the Golub-Reinsch algorithm, via the
                  modified Golub-Reinsch algorithm (faster for matrices with
                  many more rows than columns), or via a one-sided Jacobi
                  orthogonalization. See the GSL manual page on SVD.

*********** SVD's in Matlab
************* Matlab's [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/techdoc/matlab.html][economy size svd]]
*************** get econmoy size when use svd(X,0) or svd(X,'econ')
*************** when m<n, then S(k,k)=0 for k>m (eg. [[https://listserv.umd.edu/cgi-bin/wa?A2=ind9903&L=ics-l&O=A&F=P&P=2241][here]])
*************** so economy size returns and mxn U but S and V are mxm
*************** this isn't really dimension reduction
************* svds(): this computes an eigenvalue subset: it's what I want
************* see [[file:~/lib/matlab/scottlib/pcasvds.m::function%20Xproj%20meanX%20V%20S%20pcasvds%20X%20K][pcasvds.m]]
********* Different ways to calc PCA
*********** Why eigenvecs of covariance matrix?
            ([[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::duda01pattClassBook][duda et al. 2001: pattern classification]], p. 115-117)
************* want to summarize data @ least cost (min squared error)
************* _one number_ mean
************* _one line_ running through mean: largest eigenvalue of scatter
              matrix, which is (npts-1) * cov mat
************* _N lines_ N largest eigen vectors
*********** Why SVD V vector after making zero mean?
************* V'=eignenvecs(XX') if X==(X-meanX) ie. V' are the princ comps
              ([[SVD vs. PCA]] above)
*********** Why SVD of cov matrix?
************* for [[square X]]: SVD is same as diagonalization ie. solving eigenval prob
*********** Why <<<normalize by variance>>>: SVD((x-meanX)/var)?
************* just subtracting the mean gets you the covariance: you're done, right?
************* I guess the idea is to make the analysis scale independent:
              if don't divide, the just multiplying a variable (column of
              X) would change the PCA analysis.
************* So... dividing by variance is probably a good idea unless the
              variables have a physically significant scaling
*********** Cov matrix vs. mean/var data SVD
************* good [[http://eos.whoi.edu/12.747/notes/lect04/lectno04.html#PCA][explanation]] of why they're the same (actually whole
            [[http://eos.whoi.edu/12.747/notes/lect04/lectno04.html][section]] on PCA and factor analysis is good)
*********** Matlab's pca functions don't normalize by variance
************* [[file:/usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab/.2006b/toolbox/stats/princomp.m::function%20coeff%20score%20latent%20tsquare%20princomp%20x%20econFlag][princomp()]]: just (x-mean) --> SVD: V is the dim-compressed version of x
*************** they suggest princomp([[file:/usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab/.2006b/toolbox/stats/zscore.m::function%20z%20zscore%20x][zscore]](x))
************* [[file:/usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab/.2006b/toolbox/stats/pcacov.m::function%20coeff%20latent%20explained%20pcacov%20v][pcacov]](): doesn't normalize either expects raw covariance matrix (square)
*************** so... pcacov([[file:/afs/ee.washington.edu/nikola/.@sys/pkgs/matlab/.2006b/toolbox/matlab/datafun/cov.m::function%20xy%20cov%20x%20varargin][cov]](x)) wouldn't be variance normalized
*************** to normalize, they [[file:/usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab/.2006b/toolbox/stats/pcacov.m::on%20standardized%20variables%20use%20the%20correlation%20matrix%20R%20V%20SD%20SD][recommend]]:
                pcacov(V./(SD*SD'))), where SD = sqrt(diag(cov(x)))
******* Large data PCA/SVD
********* [[http://www.merl.com/publications/TR2006-059/][Fast Low-Rank Modifications of the Thin Singular Value Decomposition]]
*********** good for when data is too large for memory eg. thin SVD of video stream
*********** can do sliding window, I think
*********** operations are: update, downdate, revise, recenter
*********** This [[http://apperceptual.wordpress.com/2007/09/18/svd-and-tucker-decomposition-with-low-ram-requirements/][guy]] likes it 
************* Has implemented several other [[http://www.eecs.umich.edu/~wingated/resources.html][Incremental SVD updates]] 
*********** for big SVD, of all the data set, use [[http://www.eecs.umich.edu/~wingated/scripts/addblock_svd_update.m][addblock_svd_update()]]
********* could also use [[Probabilistic PCA]] to do reduced SVD

                the R language, along with several other algs, like NIPALS
                and nonlinear PCA)

                kind of a mix, but it isn't applied to pca).  Seems equivocl

            - [[http://portal.acm.org/citation.cfm%3Fid%3D1015418&jmp%3Dcit&coll%3DGUIDE&dl%3DGUIDE][Predictive automatic relevance determination by expectation propagation]]
            - [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/xpls/abs_all.jsp%3Farnumber%3D1659843][Automatic Relevance Determination for the Estimation of Relevant Features for Object Recognition]]
            - [[ieeexplore.ieee.org/iel5/4028925/4030573/04398660.pdf%20][Classifying ovarian tumors using Bayesian Multi-Layer Perceptrons and Automatic Relevance Determination: A multi-center study]]
            - [[http://citeseer.ist.psu.edu/617045.html][Automatic Relevance Determination for  Least Squares Support Vector Machine Classiers]]

              Reduction with Principal and Independent Component Analysis]]

      - [[http://www.nist.gov/speech/publications/papersrc/rt05sresults.pdf][RT05se details]] 

        Each meeting recording evaluation excerpt met minimum sensor
        requirements.  Each meeting participant wore a head-mounted close
        talking microphone and there were at least three table top
        microphones placed on a table between the meeting participants.
        The only exception to this is meeting NIST_20050412-1303 from NIST
        in which a meeting participant was talking over a conference
        phone. In addition to these sensors, the AMI meetings included an
        eight-channel circular microphone array placed on the table between
        the meeting participants, and the NIST meetings included three Mark
        III arrays mounted on the walls.

*********** [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::wax85sigDetInfo][Wax 1985: Detection of signals]]: degrees of freedom derivation
            AIC and MDL number degrees of freedom derivation for PCA dim pick
*********** [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Valle99pcaNcompsRecons][Valle et al. 1999: Selection of Number]]: 10 PCA dim picking techniques
*********** [[http://www.ijcai.org/papers/post-0330.pdf][BIC not identical to MDL]] (as is commonly believed)
********* highest average receive power @ beamformer output on reconstructed XC lags?
******* Variance normalize before PCA?
********* eratios: NO
*********** Close Pairs: little ratio change -- they get the same signal
*********** Far Pairs: big ratio change if different spkr loc -- important
*********** div-by-var pumps close pair noise, decreases far pair important changes
*********** So... /don't divide by variance/
*********** TODO run test experiment w/o div by variance
********* xcpairs: MAYBE
*********** Close Pairs: little delay change, also probably reliable since not noisy
*********** Far Pairs: noisy so probably lots of garbage: morm would deemphaise noise
*********** So... /may want to divide by variance/
*********** TODO try with and without normalization
********* eratios+xcpairs: SORTA, but separate streams better? ?
*********** PCA on concatenated features: must separately normalize _before_ PCA
************* Problems w/ concatenation XC and ER before PCA
              1. Different normalization required for eratios and xcpairs
                 - eratios: don't want to div-by-var (close pair noise pump)
                 - xcpairs: may want to norm but this will make xcpairs small
                   w.r.t. non-normalized eratos
              2. If only normalize xcpairs, they will be small: eratios will dominate
              3. eratios have /larger dimension/ ==> they will dominate xcpairs
*********** Separate PCA: must separately_normalize _after_ PCA, before GMM :conclusion:
************* GMM emphasizes features w/ largest dynamic range
              (conclusion from papers below)             
*************** TODO [[http://www.lia.univ-avignon.fr/fich_art/756-scheffer.pdf%20][UBM spkrID with rank normalization]] (kinda works?): good to read
                - supervised classifier: GMM posteriors --> SVM spkr ID
                - rank norm works on 128gmm, fails on 2048
                - but OK if remove lowest and highest weight GMM mixtures
*************** TODO [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/iel5/10203/32544/01521717.pdf?arnumber=1521717][Speech emotion GMM w/ linear dynrange remap]]: good to read
                - features have 10e6, 10e2 dynamic ranges
                - says, yup, bigger drange feats have more influence on GMM
                - norm depends upon feature distribution:
                  - symmetric: (0,1) scaling (min-->0, max-->1)
                  - exponential: exponential warping (Section 4), avoids
                    having most values clumped near zero (causes underflows)
*********** Separate PCA is better: (no solution for eratios dimension problem)
*********** TODO So... try this?
            1. variance normalize xcpairs
            2. PCA xcpairs
            3. PCA raw eratios
            4. Two ways to do final normalization:
               - variance normalize all (presumably previous PCA's gave
                  stuff appropriate weight)
               - /also/ PCA again (better feature reduction)

********* Experiments

          |         | pre PCA  | best | best | PCA in | post |
          | feature | norm     | dim  | nmix | merge  | PCA  |
          |---------+----------+------+------+--------+------|
          | xcpair  | no       | XX   | YY   |        |      |
          | xcpair  | yes      | XX   | YY   |        |      |
          | eratio  | no       | XX   | YY   |        |      |
          | eratio  | yes      | XX   | YY   |        |      |
          |---------+----------+------+------+--------+------|
          | XC+ER   | yes/yes  | XX   | YY   | concat | no   |
          | XC+ER   | best y/n | XX   | YY   | concat | no   |
          | XC+ER   | yes/yes  | XX   | YY   | sep    | no   |
          | XC+ER   | best y/n | XX   | YY   | sep    | no   |
          | XC+ER   | yes/yes  | XX   | YY   | concat | yes  |
          | XC+ER   | best y/n | XX   | YY   | concat | yes  |
          | XC+ER   | yes/yes  | XX   | YY   | sep    | yes  |
          | XC+ER   | best y/n | XX   | YY   | sep    | yes  |

******* Probabilistic PCA
      
      |                        |                                      | latent      |                |                                               |
      | algorithm              | input noise model                    | noise model | dim sel        | comment                                       |
      |------------------------+--------------------------------------+-------------+----------------+-----------------------------------------------|
      | Factor Analysis        | diagonal Gauss                       | Gauss       | ?              | not necess. PCA?  See [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Tipping99ProbPrincComp][Tipping99ProbPrincComp]]  |
      | [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Tipping99ProbPrincComp][PPCA]]                   | isotropic Gauss (const diag)         | Gauss       | BIC?           | the original                                  |
      | [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Sanguinetti05nppca][NPPCA]]                  | isotropic Gauss + external meas. var | Gauss       | from meas var. | meas. variance on each point, mean is est.    |
      | [[rtPPCA]]                 | Student                              | Student     |                | also CCA                                      |
      | [[Generalized PCA]] (ePCA) | Gauss,Poisson,expon,bernoulli        |             |                | handles binary, integer, positive, etc. noise |
      | [[SPCA]]                   | isotropic Gauss                      | Gauss       |                | missing values built in                       |
      | [[RPCA]]                   | ?                                    | ?           |                |                                               |
      | [[DPPCA]]                  | ?                                    | Gauss       |                | nonlinear                                     |
      
********* [[http://csdl2.computer.org/persagen/DLAbsToc.jsp?resourcePath=/dl/trans/tp/&toc=comp/trans/tp/2005/12/iztoc.xml&DOI=10.1109/TPAMI.2005.244][Generalized PCA (ePCA)]]
*********** geometrically determines # subspaces?
*********** same as PPCA if noise matched PPCA assumptions (claimed in nice [[http://cis.jhu.edu/~rvidal/publications/phdthesis.pdf][thesis]])?
*********** noise can be any exponential dist, doesn't have to be Gaussian
            eg. can handle binary, all positive noise, etc.
*********** replace max log likelihood w/ "Bregman" distance
*********** nice [[Generalized%20PCA%20slides][Generalized PCA slides]] just for PCA if nothing else.   Also, a [[http://books.nips.cc/papers/files/nips14/AA27.pdf][paper]].
********* Robust Principal Component Analysis ([[http://www.cs.brown.edu/~black/Papers/rpca.pdf][RPCA]])
*********** models intra-sample outliers
*********** has [[http://www.salle.url.edu/~ftorre/papers/rpca/rpca.zip][matlab]]
*********** not probabilistic?
********* Sensible PCA (SPCA, has matlab)
*********** seems to be Tipping's PPCA, and people seem to call it PPCA
*********** examples with npts ~ 10*nDims.
*********** see [[Matlab for Sensible PCA]]
********* NPPCA: [[http://www.dcs.shef.ac.uk/~neil/projects/pipeline/#Sanguinetti:accounting05][micro-array PPCA]] does measurement uncertainty, has [[PPCA Matlab]]
*********** uncertainty is a "variance," not a confidence
***********  _good for lag feature confidence_, not MP beamform (unless
             estimate conf for whole channel filter)
*********** pick dimension automatically from user-supplied measurement confs
***********  _better error targets_ use supervised clustered lag vector to
             measure this variance
************* cluster lags from non-overlapped segments (use CCA so get good ones)
************* error is difference from these lags: could turn into variance or confidence
************* Then, can either calc variance from error given conf features
              or predict error given conf features
********* [[http://jmlr.csail.mit.edu/papers/volume6/lawrence05a/lawrence05a.pdf][DPPCA]]: dual (nonlinear) probabilistic [[DPPCA has matlab here]]
********* Handling Non-Gaussianininity
*********** PPCA very slow if non-Gauss noise: [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::roweis98spca][roweis 1998: em algorithms for]]
*********** For xcorr lag PCA
************* xlags not Gaussian: [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Sonmez97LognormTiedMixPitch][sonmez et al. 1997: lognormal tied mixture]] ==> PPCA s/ work on log(lag)
*************** at least if use a PPCA that assumes Gaussian noise
*************** would have to add a lag offset to avoid log of <= 0
************* PPCA model is a little trickier than in Sonmez:
              
              is: lag + noise
                  noise ~= k*T0;  k=0,-1,1
                  
                  want to model pitch in log land to match Gaussianinity
                  assumpt.

                  Hmm... this isn't going anywhere but see notebook

************* [[http://www-cse.ucsd.edu/classes/fa02/cse252c/pca.pdf][Generalized PCA slides]] are a good overview of exponential noise models

*********** For [[Mixture of beamformers]]
************* speech is super-Guassian (kurtosis too big): [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::leblanc98kurtosisSep][leblanc & leon 1998: speech separation by kurtosis maximization]]
************* output of algorithm is delay-sum speech, so the model won't fit well
************* [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/iel5/97/27108/01203784.pdf?arnumber=1203784][Laplace]] or [[http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1974STIN...7520587Z][Gamma]] (or only [[http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sites/entrez?cmd=Retrieve&db=PubMed&list_uids=3794063&dopt=Abstract][Gamma for rectified?]]) do [[http://www.hindawi.com/GetPDF.aspx?doi=10.1155/ASP.2005.1110][fit speech better]] (generalized gaussian?)
************* Could use rtPPCA: does Student's-t fit?
*************** kurtoisis is an adustable [[http://mathworld.wolfram.com/Studentst-Distribution.html][parameter]] but tied to variance
************* [[Generalized PCA]] does exponential distributions, [[http://www.casact.org/pubs/dpp/dpp04/04dpp117.pdf][Gamma is expon. dist]]
********* Matlab code for PPCA
*********** [[http://lear.inrialpes.fr/~verbeek/software][Mixture of Factor Analyzers]] which is mix of PPCA if set to isotropic noise
*********** [[http://lear.inrialpes.fr/~verbeek/software][Matlab for Sensible PCA]] (SPCA, Probabilistic PCA with missing values)
************* missing values are missing or not (binary presence), extend to confs?
************* complexity is O(numEigsComputed*numPts*numInputDim)
*************** normal PCA covariance calc not done here is O(numPts*numInputDim^2)
*************** speed: On a real vision problem with missing information, I
                have computed the leading eigenvectors and eigenvalues of 2^17
                points in 2^12 dimensions in a few hours using MATLAB on a modest
                workstation (in 1998!)

#include <iostream>
#include <boost/numeric/bindings/lapack/gesdd.hpp>
 #include<boost/numeric/bindings/traits/ublas_matrix.hpp>

  matrix<double> A (4,2);
 A(0,0)=2;
 A(0,1)=4;
 A(1,0)=1;
 A(1,1)=3;
 A(2,0)=0;
 A(2,1)=0;
 A(3,0)=0;
 A(3,1)=0;
 print_matrix(A);

 matrix<double> V(2,2);
  vector<double> S(8);

 return 0;

Message: 2
Date: Fri, 27 May 2005 08:23:29 +0200
From: Kresimir Fresl <fresl@master.grad.hr>
Subject: Re: [ublas] svd example program
To: ublas mailing list <ublas@lists.boost.org>
Message-ID: <4296BCE1.9010105@master.grad.hr>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii; format=flowed


Hi Jack,

you wrote:


>> I use g++ an got a bunch of errors. I think I m not including proper
>> libs or I m not linking the correct libs. Any help is appreciated.


>> #include <iostream>
>> #include <boost/numeric/bindings/lapack/gesdd.hpp>
>> #include<boost/numeric/bindings/traits/ublas_matrix.hpp>
>> #include<boost/numeric/bindings/traits/ublas_vector.hpp>
>> #include <boost/numeric/ublas/matrix.hpp>
>> #include <boost/numeric/ublas/vector.hpp>
>> #include "printmatrix.hpp"
>> 
>> using namespace boost::numeric::bindings::lapack;
>> using namespace boost::numeric::ublas;
>> // using namespace std;
>> using namespace print;
>> int main () {
>> 
>>  matrix<double> A (4,2);


To use Lapack routines your matrices must be column major:

     matrix<double, column_major> A (4,2);


>>  A(0,0)=2;
>>  A(0,1)=4;
>>  A(1,0)=1;
>>  A(1,1)=3;
>>  A(2,0)=0;
>>  A(2,1)=0;
>>  A(3,0)=0;
>>  A(3,1)=0;
>>  print_matrix(A);
>> 
>>  matrix<double> U(4,4);
>>  matrix<double> V(2,2);


     matrix<double, column_major> U (4,4);
     matrix<double, column_major> V (2,2);


>>  vector<double> S(8);
>>  gesdd(&A,&S,&U,&V);


There's no need for dereferencing (bindings do it for you ;o):

     gesdd (A, S, U, V);


>> //   print_matrix(S);
>> //   print_matrix(U);
>> //   print_matrix(V);
>> 
>>  return 0;
>> }


For more info see examples in

     http://tinyurl.com/ccmwa

and docs in

     http://tinyurl.com/6acht

(BTW, I didn't update ublas and bindings on my machine for
some time. I think that in the meantime interface of ublas
slightly changed, so there may be some more errors, but I
hope that this helps.)

Regards,

fres

*********** [[http://www.comp-phys.org:16080/software/ietl/][IETL Project]]: Iterative Eigensolver (big eigen problems eg. PCA,CCA)
************* Methods
              - Power method
              - Inverse iteration
              - Rayleigh quotients
              - Lanczos algorithm without reorthogonalization in the
                formulation of Cullum and Willoughby [3,4]

********* Reading/Writing .mat data files in C
*********** Creating a MAT-File in C ([[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/techdoc/matlab.html][Matlab Tutorial]])
************* [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/techdoc/matlab_external/f19027.html][Compiling matlab]]: Compile Matlab's test program using mex to see what the gcc options are
************* Compiling w/ makefile commands instead of using mex

              cp /usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab/extern/examples/eng_mat/matcreat.c .

              use -n to print out the gcc commands
              mex -n -f /usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab/bin/matopts.sh  matcreat.c

              The output can be simplified to (assuming LD_LIBRARY_PATH IS
              SET CORRECTLY):

              set MROOT=/usr/nikola/pkgs/matlab
              set MLINKOpts=-I$(MROOT)/extern/include -I$(MROOT)/simulink/include -DMATLAB_MEX_FILE -ansi -D_GNU_SOURCE -fexceptions  -DMX_COMPAT_32 -O -DNDEBUG
              gcc -c $(MLINKOpts) matcreat.c

              gcc -c $(MLINKOpts) $(MROOT)/extern/src/mexversion.c

              gcc -O  -o matcreat  matcreat.o mexversion.o  -Wl,-rpath-link,$(MROOT)/bin/glnx86 -L$(MROOT)/bin/glnx86 -lmat -lmx -lm -lstdc++
              
              I tried it on the command line ($()-->$) and it worked

*************** C++ representation of stuff to be converted to .mat file

                | C++ type                                    | matlab type |
                |---------------------------------------------+-------------|
                | vector<numeric types>                       | array       |
                | [[http://www.boost.org/doc/html/array.html][boost::array]] (multi-dim, dims don't change) | array       |
                | [[http://www.boost.org/libs/multi_array/doc/index.html][boost::multi_array]] (multi, variable dims)   | array       |
                | map<> of *void elements                     | struct      |
                | map of [[http://www.boost.org/doc/html/any.html][boost::any]]                           | struct      |
                | map of [[http://www.boost.org/doc/html/any.html][boost::variant]]                       | struct      |
                | vector<string>                              | cell        |
                | vector/multi_array of *void                 | cell        |
                | vector/array/multi_array of [[http://www.boost.org/doc/html/any.html][boost::any]]      | cell        |
                | vector/array/multi_array of [[http://www.boost.org/doc/html/any.html][boost::variant]]  | cell        |

***** Non-negative matrix factorization (NNMF)
******* Why?
********* reduces dim and ensures that transforming matrix is all positive
          ==> confidences will be weighted according to strength of
          transform and will remain positive!
********* Is "place-based",
*********** images are spatially segregated eg. chin eyes, etc..
*********** like speech over time?
************* only one D instead of 2-D (D is time)
************* at one time, speech only from one person (except in overlaps)
************* TODO NNMF map over time
********* can this be combined w/ CCA?
********* can this be combined w/ Bayesian PCA?
********* can this replace SVD in maximum power beamforming?

*********** problem is that initialization is random: I get only one chance
********* [[http://www.cs.helsinki.fi/u/phoyer/][Matlab]] for Sparse NNMF (nmfpack, 2004, updated 2006)
*********** [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Hoyer04NNMFsparseConstr][hoyer 2004: non negative matrix]]
*********** functions:
            nmfdiv.m       - performs standard NMF with divergence objective
            nmfmse.m       - performs standard NMF with euclidean objective
            nmfsc.m        - performs NMF with sparseness constraints
            lnmf.m         - performs Local NMF
            snmf.m         - performs Sparse NMF

********* [[http://www.broad.mit.edu/mpr/publications/projects/NMF/nmf.m][Brunet Divergence]] Matlab implementation
*********** minimizes "divergence"
************* divergence is the divergence equation between the original
              and approximated data matrices (which must be normalized to
              sum to one so they are like prob distributions)
*********** is multiplicative (means it can get stuck in zeros)
*********** For my data, the compression is not very sparse ([[file:~/meetings/xclust/test/nnmf_test.m][nnmf_test.m]])
***********[[http://hebb.mit.edu/people/seung/papers/nmfconverge.pdf%20][ paper]]

******* Multi-way CCA (more than just a pair)
********* may not need if do [[Two step CCA]] (fuse ER/XC, then MFCC posteriors)
********* but in general, need to do multiway, not serial 2-way (see OneNote notes on home PC)
*********** CCA transforms are invertible ==> each CCA in chain can undo the last one
*********** could reduce dims
*********** some dim reduction inevitable for non-matching dims 
            dim(output) == min(rank(X1),rank(x1))
*********** to avoid undesirable info loss, need to CCA highest dims 1st
********* wouldn't want to use MFCC's directly, instead use vector of post. probs
*********** need more MFCC mixtures/time for good MFCC training
*********** may want to associate more than one location (fused ER/XC)
            to an MFCC
*********** Two step CCA approach?
            1. Cluster normally
            2. build MFCC speaker ID models
            3. maybe build location models on fused location features
            4. CCA-fuse mfcc posteriors/locations, allows >1 loc to be
               correlated w/ a speaker
            5. cluster again (how handle non-speech?)
********* [[http://www.sciencedirect.com.offcampus.lib.washington.edu/science?_ob=ArticleURL&_udi=B6T08-4MC71HN-1&_user=582538&_coverDate=01%2F31%2F2007&_rdoc=15&_fmt=summary&_orig=browse&_srch=doc-info(%23toc%234856%232007%23999799998%23640153%23FLA%23display%23Volume)&_cdi=4856&_sort=d&_docanchor=&view=c&_ct=16&_acct=C000029718&_version=1&_urlVersion=0&_userid=582538&md5=3b00d55ab5d51b8ce905570d395c6285][Neural CCA]] (2007)
*********** (adaptive) don't need to calc covariance matrix

*********** D. Hardoon's [[http://homepage.mac.com/davidrh/_html/code.html][KCCA package]] (downloaded [[file:~/lib/matlab/kcca_package][here]])
************* [[http://homepage.mac.com/davidrh/_papers/TR_CSD_03_02.pdf][Tech Note]] is a nice all-in-one explanation of
              - CCA-->KCCA
              - regularization
              - Partial Grahm Schmidt orthogonalization (PSGO)
              - Cholesky decomp (full and incomplete)
              - better than my book ([[http://www.kernel-methods.net/][Kernel Methods for Pattern Analysis]])? 
************* Tech Note coauthor is author of [[http://www.kernel-methods.net/][Kernel Methods for Pattern Analysis]]
************* Regularization simpler than in  [[http://www.kernel-methods.net/][Kernel Methods for Pattern Analysis]]
************* Doesn't need full kernels if:
              1. [[file:~/lib/matlab/kcca_package/kcanonca_reg_ver2.m::disp%20Decomposing%20Kernel%20with%20PGSO][precompute]] partial cholesky (PSGO?) kernel decomps for two views
              2. have already centered the data (and comment out [[file:~/lib/matlab/kcca_package/kcanonca_reg_ver2.m::If%20you%20centre%20outside%20comment%20out%20this%20bit][centering code]])
              3. don't use [[file:~/lib/matlab/kcca_package/kcanonca_reg_ver2.m::Ax%20Kx%20nalpha][nor==1]] (GS projected space [[file:~/lib/matlab/kcca_package/kcanonca_reg_ver2.m::1%20No%20normalisation%20and%20and%20leaving%20GS%20projected%20space][left alone]])

******* CCA relationship to Gaussian Information Bottlneck
        GIB: compress two views to a single one that doesn't lose
        information.  GIB assumes that the signals are Gauassian (normally,
        IB assumes discrete variables).  GIB is closely related to CCA, but
        eigen vector weights (estimates of significant realtionships might
        be different).

******** Gaussian information bottleneck papers ([[http://www.robotics.stanford.edu/~gal/ps_files/chechik_nips2003IBWorkshop.ppt][slides]], and [[http://people.csail.mit.edu/~gamir/pubs/Chechik_JMLR2004.pdf][paper]]) 
******** [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::seldin07infoBottleneckNonCoOccur][Seldin et al. 2007: Information bottleneck for]] suggests similar dim reduce in future work

*********  _Relevant Canonical Correlation Analysis_

******* CCA is almost the same as max power beamforming
********* one pair CCA
          1.take a mic pair
          2.make a matrix of lag-shifted copies of the signals
          3.do CCA
********* the "most correlated" projection will be @ the right delay, w/ weights
******* CCA could be a "maximum correlation beamformer"
********* different from max power
********* set up two "views" composed of lags such that every pair is
          compared against every other (like that one Chinese guy's paper,
          w/ words in a documnent?)
********* over a time window, say 1s, project in max correlation direction.
          Topmost correlated CCA dims become the input to the HMM.  
*********  _waitaminute!_ this can't work!  The projection would change
           every window.  Can only work if there is a mixture of CCA
           transforms, like the mixture of PCA stuff!

        each other: /unlikely/)

*** What is a speaker ID error?
***** Two types:
      1. gets the wrong speaker when there is true speech (like in RTTM segs)
      2. tries to get a speaker ID when there is no speech (false VAD)
***** DONE Include VAD errors in the confidence training (Mari suggestion)
******* Good idea: could make confidence similar to Xavi's purification stuff
******* Xavi's [[file:/g/ssli/data/meetings/acoustic/spkrseg_loc/xavi/mdm/spnsp/CMU_20020319-1400.spch][.spch]] VAD files are fed into the clustering prog via [[file:~/meetings/xclust/xclust.pl::spnsp_file%20clustFeat%20in%20mtng%20feat%20spnsp_spch][--spnsp_file]] 
********* Xavi's VAD is very coarse, like min size==3s or something
          ==> if used them in cheating experiments, would have tons of errors
******* GMM speaker ID error target generation (makes MLP isErr training targets)
********* GMM train (target generation)
*********** want to train w/ nonspeech VAD frames, like in real life
************* so, use Xavi's .spch file (his VAD)
************* clustering eventually gets good speaker ID ==> rttm's are
              reasonable /but/ for _false VAD_ (.spch and !rttm), must define
              which speaker should get the data.  So...
************* Speaker GMM training data:
              1. all _rttm data within .spch_
              2. false VAD frames (.spch && !rttm) for which it is "closest" spkr
                 - "closest": convolve each spkr VAD waveform w/ LPF, assign
                   false VAD frame to spkr w/ max filter response (see
                   notebook, 2/13/07)
********* GMM eval (target generation)
*********** know exactly where false VAD's are: don't need to estimate them
*********** ideally, clusterer would "reject" bad frames, but that's not in
            Xavi's algorithm
            ==> the big effect of confidence would show up on cluster training
*********** So, _eval on rttm segs_, find errors there, and then _add_ false
            VAD detects since they are errors that s/ have zero conf.
******* MLP training
********* want MLP to detect any kind of error that will be seen by clusterer
********* So, train on _all frames in .spch_ file in training
********* frame is error if:
          - .spch && !rttm
          - .spch && rttm && misclassified speaker
          (!.spch && rttm won't occur in real life: cluster won't ever see it)
********* Report three kinds of error detection mistakes
          1. total errors: missed false VAD or missed spkrID error in rttm speech
          2. missed false VAD alone
          3. missed speaker ID error during rttm speech
******* Cheating evaluation algorithm
********* GMM train
*********** same as during error target training, since is the real usage case
********* GMM eval
*********** only on RTTM's since there is no correct answer for false VAD
