      |----------------------------------+------+----+----+---------------+------+------+----+-------+-----------------|
      | max norm xcorr peak              |      |  0 |  1 | nPairs*nBands | 1    |    1 | x  |     1 | xcpair/xcollect |
      | eratio variance for strong sigs  | x    |  1 |  1 | nPairs*nBAnds | 1    |    1 | x  |     1 | eratio/ecollect |
      | xcorr harmonicity                | x    |  0 |  1 | nPairs        | T    |    2 |    |     0 | xcpair          |
      | delay triplet zero sum           |      |  0 |  1 | nPairs        | T    |    2 |    |     0 | xcpair/xcollect |
      | xcorr peak ratio                 | x    |  0 |  1 | nPairs        | T    |    1 | x  |     0 | xcpair          |
      | norm xcorr peak mag              | x    |  0 |  1 | nPairs        | T    |    1 | x  |     0 | xcpair          |
      | num prominent xcorr peaks        | x    |  0 |  1 | nPairs        | T    |    1 | x  |     0 | xcpair          |
      | pair spectral evelope sim.       |      |  0 |  1 | nPairs        | T    |    2 |    |     0 | xcpair          |
      | sub-band similarity              |      |  1 |  1 | nPairs*6      | T    |    2 |    |     0 | xcpair          |
      | sub-band xcorr similarity        |      |  1 |  1 | nPairs*3      | T    |    2 |    |     0 | xcpair          |

      time dep:   1==>constant, T==>timedependent
      dimension:  number of vector dimenions for this feature

***** Energy Ratio Confidences
******* low max energy:  both numerator and denominator small ==> noise vulerability
********* normalization

          N(k)           = min(energy percentile across meeting, all bands)
          confFeat(band) = max(E1(band)/N(1),E2(band)/N(2))

*********** different gains on different channels but noise floor is same
*********** ==> must be normalized relative to noise floor
*********** detect noise by finding quiet parts of meeting (bottom 10%?)
*********** want to detect if mic is in a reverb hole @ a given freq
            ==> meeting-wide low energy is total, across all bands
*********** must avoid error if channel is not plugged in during part of
            meeting (stuck at zero or const)
************* calc thresh only during UEM region?
************* reject
*********** From [[file:~/doc/bib/speakerClust.bib::Pfau01MultispeakerSpeechActivity][pfau et al. 2001: multispeaker speech activity]]:
************* The total loudness and the modified loudness are normalized
              using the overall maximum within each channel.
*************  The log-energy Ej(n) of channel j at frame n is normalized by:
*************** First, the minimum frame energy Emin,j of channel j is subtracted
                from the current energy value Ej(i) to compensate for the different
                channel gains. The minimum frame energy is used as an estimate
                of the noise floor to make this normalization mostly independent
                of the proportion of speech activity in that channel.
*************** In the second step the mean (log) energy of all M channels is
                subtracted.  This procedure is based on the idea that when a
                single signal appears in all the channels, the log energy in
                each channel will be the energy of that signal plus a
                constant term accounting for the linear gain coupling between
                that channel and the signal source.  Subtracting the average
                of all channels should remove the variation due to the
                absolute signal level, leaving a normalized energy which
                reflects solely the relative gain of the source at channel j
                compared to the average across all channels. Signals that
                occur only in one channel, such as microphone contact and
                breath noise, should also be easy to distinguish by this
                measure, since in this case the relative gain will appear
                abnormally large for the local microphone

******* entropy of model fit:
********* does this ER vector match some commonly observed model?
********* idea is that noise will be random and won't fit any model too well
********* train a GMM on all meeting speech and then calc entropy of the component posteriors
********* _problem_ for ER, cheating experiments show that you need a _mixture_
          ==> posteriors of a mixture comp won't mean much 
          but maybe that's OK. It should still fit only a few
********* _alternative_ use GMM and then dimension reduce w/ kmeans
          1. train a big GMM (UBM), lots of mixtures, say nmixERfeat*nSpkrs 
          2. k-means clustering down to nSpkrs 
          3. conf feature is the entropy of fit to each k-means cluster
          /note/ could do another GMM on the posteriors instead of using k-means

      - currently, the final, confidence-weighted GMM's are tested on the
        same data upon which the error predictor was originally trained.
        - this is because matlab restarts the rand() state to the same point
          each time its started.
      - ideally would like to test MLP on a completely new data set upon
        which it was not trained, but there are many speakers that don't
        have enough data for that, assuming you need 30s of training data
      - could do rand('state',sum(100*clock)) @ top of mkConfTrnDat.m
      - *Better* generate test/train data once and pass out the HTK files
        to mkConfTrnTest/MLP/mkConfTrnTest.  

        _Data sets:_
        1. train, single pair no conf GMM (10s==>1000 samps)
           - can be shorter since fewer mixtures, lower dim, esp. for
             xcpairs, which are 1-D
        2. test, single pair no conf GMM (10s, is also MLP train)
           - can be somewhat shorter since is test and since MLP train
             takes all pairs in series, although they are full-Dim conf feats)
        3. test, single pair conf MLP (40s, is allpair GMM test and train)
           - must be bigger since is full-DIM GMM training input and also
             full conf dim MLP training input
        4. train, all pair conf GMM (must be longest, say 30s)
           - take disjoint subset of conf MLP test
        5. test, all pair conf GMM (shorter, say 10s)
           - take disjoint subset of conf MLP test

***** TODO separate # of mixtures for single pair and all pair GMM trainings
      - ER may be failing b/c it's got 20 mixtues to work with on a single pair
        ==> over training
        ==> could have memorized data so effectively that no conf feats
            could hint
***** TODO separate MLP training steps from GMM training steps for faster runs
***** DONE cheating experiment: separate test/train in self-GMM
******* Goals:
********* Speaker ID error generating GMM
*********** separate test/train sets ie. no training dat in test
************* makes non-confidence data look worse in comparison to
              confidence data, since won't be memorizing errors that will
              also show up in test
************* makes speaker ID errors more realistic ==> better speaker
              error predictor performance, hopefully.
************* _overlaps_
*************** train: OK for all speakers in an overlap to have it in their trn dat
*************** test: error will always occur, since only one speaker is maxLik
*********** training data balanced across speakers (so one doesn't have much
            better data than the others, thus skewing error results)
*********** want to output balanced speaker ID data too:
************* the true answers should be balanced across speakers
************* respect prior prob of error?  Or balanced error/not error...
********* MLP training
*********** use the isErr training targets as they come.  Presumably, errors
            will be somewhat rare, thus avoiding training the priors of which
            would yield a confidence that zeros everything out
***** DONE Cheating experiment truth should be one-against-all?
******* N-level classifier may be too hard to learn
******* always binary so p(fail) may be less proportial to # speakers?
******* get more training data:
********* single #speakers-way classifier: one data stream per band
********* #speakers binary clasifiers: #speakers streams per band
******* *NO* I decided that this didn't work better than all-against-all
        (better speaker ID results)

******* insert confidences into GMM M step:
********* EM algorithm
          x    = mixture membership indicator
          y    = sample
          c(y) = confidence of sample y
          
          u    = sum(P(x|y)*y)/sum(x)
          var  = sum(P(x|y)*(y-u)^2)/sum(x)
          P(x) = sum(P(x|y))/sum(sum(P(x|y))) [a little garbled]

********* Adding confidences:

          just replace P(x|y) with P(X|y)*c(y)

* Test Plan & Data
*** Dev and Test Corpora

I think I remember Xavi saying that ICSI used RT02* data for their meeting
development work.  There are an extra 12 meetings in RT02 but I'm not sure
if ICSI ever ran their noise reducer over them (I need noise-reduced
waveforms to make the baseline comparison).  At least I can't find them.

Noise reduced files do exist for the RT05dev set, but these meetings were
collected with microphone arrays or microphones in manniquen heads -- not
representative of the ad-hoc microphone placement I'm interested in.

So, I think I'll use just the corpora in the table below:

I'm not sure which corpus to use as the final test set.  It's tempting to
use RT06 since it's newest, and since it has meetings from new sites, but
there is an overabundance of meetings with only 2 or 4 microphones. To get
the most diversity, in the test corpus, the best solution might be to
randomly pick one meeting from each site:

***** Test Corpus

| original corpus | meeting             | numChans | numSpkrs |
|-----------------+---------------------+----------+----------|
| rt04se          | ICSI\_20011030-1030 |        6 |       10 |
| rt04s           | LDC\_20011116-1400  |        8 |        3 |
| rt04se          | NIST\_20030925-1517 |        7 |        4 |
| rt05se          | CMU\_20050301-1415  |        3 |        4 |
| rt05se          | VT\_20050304-1300   |        2 |        5 |
| rt05se          | AMI\_20041210-1052  |       12 |        4 |
| rt06e           | EDI\_20050216-1051  |        2 |        ? |
| rt06e           | TNO\_20041103-1130  |        2 |        ? |

The other meetings would be the dev corpus.  I will probably need to split
the dev corpus into smaller sub sections, for example, train and test sets
for confidence neural nets. Comments in ICSI directories indicate that, for
the RT06 evals, they used RT05se for "tuning" and the rest for train.  I'm
not sure what that means, but possibly, the confidence neural net split
would be analagous.

*** Immediate Experimental Questions

These are questions left in the Interspeech paper aftermath

***** What is the best minimum clustering speaker duration for baseline system
      
      Grid search to find best duration on Xavi baseline system

***** What is the best XC analysis window for Hilbert/Inverse features

      Grid search using baseline best duration, with and without NR.  Use
      Xavi's single reference channel approach.

***** Does Inverse filtering work better with GCC-PHAT?
      
      Inverse filter waveforms before feeding them into Xavi's baseline, best
      duration settings
      
***** Does Inverse filtering + Hilbert transform work better than GCC-PHAT?

      Extract Xavi's features, compare with mine, using his ref chan.  Use
      duration given above.

***** Does All-pairs work better than single reference channels?

******* With no other processing?

        My XC features, best params, all channels vs. Xavi's single ref.
        
******* With ER on separate stream?

        Same experiment as above, ER on separate channel

******* With ER CCA'ed to XC, single stream

        I'm getting promising initial results by replacing PCA with canonical
        correlation analysis.  Maybe the ER / XC combo will be more powerful
        when XC is allpairs

******* With confidences?

        This is where I expect allpairs to prove superior, but I haven't come
        up with a good-enough confidence estimator yet.

        * From the README:


        /n/banquet/da/xanguera/MeetingEval06/dev_data/README:

        Development data for the 2006 NIST Meeting Evaluation. 

        rt02dev/		- Dev data from the 2002 Rich Transcription evaluation.
        rt02eval/		- Eval data from the 2002 Rich Transcription evaluation.
        rt04seval/		- Evaluation data from the RT-2004 NIST Meeting Evaluation.
        rt05sdev/		- Dev data from the RT-2005 NIST Meeting Evaluation.
        rt05seval/		- Evaluation data from the RT-2005 NIST Meeting Evaluation.

        rt02dev, rt02eval, and rt04seval are symbolic links to the directories
        created during the 2005 evaluation preparations

        rt05sdev transcript files point to the most recent processed transcript files I
        found. Its audio point to the wiener filtered waveforms under processed dir in
        MeetingEval05 dir.

        rt05seval audio points to the wavfile_nr under the MeetingEval05 dir. I copied 
        the transcript file I had from Andreas, which I copied from SRI.

********* conf test/train

          Ideally, this would be a meeting set entirely separate from the
          full speaker clustering dev set, but I am too short on meetings
          for that.  I can still test to see if this works by using the
          test set.

          Conf sets (sub-partitions of the dev set)

          | purpose                           | partition | comments                                                        | dim      |
          |-----------------------------------+-----------+-----------------------------------------------------------------+----------|
          | speaker GMM train                 | confDev   | medium large since training, but it's only 1-3 Dim              | 1 pair   |
          | speaker GMM test / conf MLP train | confDev   | same meetings, different times since is speakerID test-on-train | 1 pair   |
          | conf MLP test (speaker GMM train) | confTest  | must be large for good speaker ID on large D features           | allpairs |
          | conf MLP test (speaker GMM test)  | confTest  | same meetings, just different times                             | allpairs |

*** Significance Testing
***** Background: Matched Pair Tests
******* Student T matched pair test

        Performs a paired t-test of the null hypothesis that data in the
        difference x-y are a random sample from a normal distribution with
        mean 0 and unknown variance, against the alternative that the mean
        is not 0. (from matlab)

********* Assumes normal distribution
********* Numerical Recipies, p. 618, explains why paired match is best
********* Matlab function: [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/index.html%3F/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/ttest.html&http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/signrank.html][ttest]]
******* Wilcoxon signed-rank test (Matlab function: [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/index.html%3F/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/signrank.html&http://www.google.com/search%3Fhl%3Den&client%3Dfirefox-a&rls%3Dorg.mozilla%3Aen-US%3Aofficial&q%3Dmatlab%2Bstatistics%2Btoolbox%2B%22wilcoxon&btnG%3DSearch][signrank]])

        Performs a paired, two-sided signed rank test of the null
        hypothesis that data in the vector x-y come from a continuous,
        symmetric distribution with zero median, against the alternative
        that the distribution does not have zero median. x (from matlab)

********* nonparameteric (doesn't assume normal)
********* Example of use: [[http://www.jbjs.org.uk/cgi/content/full/87-B/11/1468%3Fck%3Dnck][oxygen concentration in hip joints after surgery]]
********* Supposed to be more sensitive than student-t for small numbers

          From [[http://dbigbear.blogspot.com/2007/08/wilcoxon-signed-rank-test-wilcoxon-rank.html][here]]:

          A nonparametric alternative to the paired t-test which is similar
          to the Fisher sign test, but it is much more sensitive. In fact,
          for large numbers it is almost as sensitive as the Student
          t-test. *For small numbers with unknown distributions this test is*
          *even more sensitive than the Student t-test.* As it is only on
          rare occasions that we do know that values are Normal
          distributed, this test is to be *preferred over the Student*
          *t-test*. This test assumes that there is information in the
          magnitudes of the differences between paired observations, as
          well as the signs.

******* Wilcoxon rank-sum test (Matlab function: [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/index.html%3F/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/ranksum.html&http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/signrank.html][ranksum]])
        
        Performs a two-sided rank sum test of the null hypothesis that data
        in the vectors x and y are independent samples from identical
        continuous distributions with equal medians, against the
        alternative that they do not have equal medians.(from matlab)

********* nonparametric (doesn't assume normality)
******* Z-test (Matlab [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/index.html%3F/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/ztest.html&http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/signrank.html][ztest]]

        Performs a z-test of the null hypothesis that data in the vector x
        are a random sample from a normal distribution with mean m and
        standard deviation sigma, against the alternative that the mean is
        not m.

        * assumes normality
        * not as good as T-test b/c mean estimate is assumed accurate.  I
          think that the ttest assumes that the dist of either
          distribution is measured, with some error

***** Significance Results
******* Table 4-2: Error vs. Features and Dimension Reduction

        Retrieve thesis.lyx version 1.4, the last version w/ run #'s.  Then
        run statistical significance between the experiments, using
        [[file:~/meetings/xclust/sigtests.m::test%20significance%20of%20results%20in%20thesis%20table%204%202][sigtest.m]]
        
        Expt. 2 in v1.4 and the thesis I presented to the committee had a
        dev meeting instead of a test.  It also seems like PCA(XC)/PCA(ER)
        on separate HMM streams got good results, at least better than what
        was listed in the table.  So, I used that for my final thesis draft
        and changed the thesis wording to say that weights were set to 0
        for some feature combinatations containing energy.
